65→/**\n    66→ * A component that provides a {@link #context() StateStoreContext} that can be supplied to a {@link KeyValueStore} so that\n    67→ * all entries written to the Kafka topic by the store during {@link KeyValueStore#commit(Map)} are captured for testing purposes.\n    68→ * This class simplifies testing of various {@link KeyValueStore} instances, especially those that use\n    69→ * {@link MeteredKeyValueStore} to monitor and write its entries to the Kafka topic.\n    70→ *\n    71→ * <h2>Basic usage</h2>\n    72→ * This component can be used to help test a {@link KeyValueStore}'s ability to read and write entries.\n    73→ *\n    74→ * <pre>\n    75→ * // Create the test driver ...\n    76→ * KeyValueStoreTestDriver&lt;Integer, String> driver = KeyValueStoreTestDriver.create();\n    77→ * KeyValueStore&lt;Integer, String> store = Stores.create(\"my-store\", driver.context())\n    78→ *                                              .withIntegerKeys().withStringKeys()\n    79→ *                                              .inMemory().build();\n    80→ *\n    81→ * // Verify that the store reads and writes correctly ...\n    82→ * store.put(0, \"zero\");\n    83→ * store.put(1, \"one\");\n    84→ * store.put(2, \"two\");\n    85→ * store.put(4, \"four\");\n    86→ * store.put(5, \"five\");\n    87→ * assertEquals(5, driver.sizeOf(store));\n    88→ * assertEquals(\"zero\", store.get(0));\n    89→ * assertEquals(\"one\", store.get(1));\n    90→ * assertEquals(\"two\", store.get(2));\n    91→ * assertEquals(\"four\", store.get(4));\n    92→ * assertEquals(\"five\", store.get(5));\n    93→ * assertNull(store.get(3));\n    94→ * store.delete(5);\n    95→ *\n    96→ * // Commit the store and verify all current entries were properly committed ...\n    97→ * store.commit(Map.of());\n    98→ * assertEquals(\"zero\", driver.committedEntryStored(0));\n    99→ * assertEquals(\"one\", driver.committedEntryStored(1));\n   100→ * assertEquals(\"two\", driver.committedEntryStored(2));\n   101→ * assertEquals(\"four\", driver.committedEntryStored(4));\n   102→ * assertNull(driver.committedEntryStored(5));\n   103→ *\n   104→ * assertEquals(false, driver.committedEntryRemoved(0));\n   105→ * assertEquals(false, driver.committedEntryRemoved(1));\n   106→ * assertEquals(false, driver.committedEntryRemoved(2));\n   107→ * assertEquals(false, driver.committedEntryRemoved(4));\n   108→ * assertEquals(true, driver.committedEntryRemoved(5));\n   109→ * </pre>\n   110→ *\n   111→ *\n   112→ * <h2>Restoring a store</h2>\n   113→ * This component can be used to test whether a {@link KeyValueStore} implementation properly\n   114→ * {@link StateStoreContext#register(StateStore, StateRestoreCallback) registers itself} with the {@link StateStoreContext}, so that\n   115→ * the persisted contents of a store are properly restored from the committed entries when the store instance is started.\n   116→ * <p>\n   117→ * To do this, create an instance of this driver component, {@link #addEntryToRestoreLog(Object, Object) add entries} that will be\n   118→ * passed to the store upon creation (simulating the entries that were previously committed to the topic), and then create the store\n   119→ * using this driver's {@link #context() ProcessorContext}:\n   120→ *\n   121→ * <pre>\n   122→ * // Create the test driver ...\n   123→ * KeyValueStoreTestDriver&lt;Integer, String> driver = KeyValueStoreTestDriver.create(Integer.class, String.class);\n   124→ *\n   125→ * // Add any entries that will be restored to any store that uses the driver's context ...\n   126→ * driver.addRestoreEntry(0, \"zero\");\n   127→ * driver.addRestoreEntry(1, \"one\");\n   128→ * driver.addRestoreEntry(2, \"two\");\n   129→ * driver.addRestoreEntry(4, \"four\");\n   130→ *\n   131→ * // Create the store, which should register with the context and automatically\n   132→ * // receive the restore entries ...\n   133→ * KeyValueStore&lt;Integer, String> store = Stores.create(\"my-store\", driver.context())\n   134→ *                                              .withIntegerKeys().withStringKeys()\n   135→ *                                              .inMemory().build();\n   136→ *\n   137→ * // Verify that the store's contents were properly restored ...\n   138→ * assertEquals(0, driver.checkForRestoredEntries(store));\n   139→ *\n   140→ * // and there are no other entries ...\n   141→ * assertEquals(4, driver.sizeOf(store));\n   142→ * </pre>\n   143→ *\n   144→ * @param <K> the type of keys placed in the store\n   145→ * @param <V> the type of values placed in the store\n   146→ */\n   147→public Do NOT call `context.restore()` yet\n\n**Execution Phase (Concurrent):**\n```java\n// Thread 1: Normal puts\nnew Thread(() -> {\n    for (int i = 0; i < 100; i++) {\n        store.put(key1, \"value\" + i);\n        store.put(key2, \"value\" + i);\n    }\n}).start();\n\n// Thread 2: Trigger restore\nnew Thread(() -> {\n    context.restore(store.name(), driver.restoredEntries());\n}).start();\n\n// Wait and verify consistency\nThread.sleep(500);\n```\n\n---\n\n### 8. **Mock Context Methods for Testing**\n\n**InternalMockProcessorContext (Better for complete context):**\n- `restore(storeName, changeLog)` - Trigger restore from KeyValue pairs\n- `restoreWithHeaders(storeName, changeLog)` - Trigger restore from ConsumerRecords\n- `stateRestoreCallback(storeName)` - Get the callback after registration\n- `register(store, callback)` - Manual registration if needed\n\n---\n\n### 9. **Complete Test Example Pattern**\n\nFrom `InMemoryKeyValueStoreTest.java:102-118`:\n\n```java\n@Test\npublic void shouldRemoveKeysWithNullValues() {\n    store.close();\n    \n    // Pre-add restore entries\n    driver.addEntryToRestoreLog(0, \"zero\");\n    driver.addEntryToRestoreLog(1, \"one\");\n    driver.addEntryToRestoreLog(2, \"two\");\n    driver.addEntryToRestoreLog(3, \"three\");\n    driver.addEntryToRestoreLog(0, null);  // Tombstone/deletion\n    \n    // Create store (registers restore callback)\n    store = createKeyValueStore(driver.context());\n    \n    // Trigger restore callback\n    context.restore(store.name(), driver.restoredEntries());\n    \n    // Verify results\n    assertEquals(3, driver.sizeOf(store));\n    assertThat(store.get(0), nullValue());  // Tombstone worked\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Summary of Key Files to Reference\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Methods |\n|------|---------|-------------|\n| `InMemoryKeyValueStoreTest.java` | Main tests for in-memory store | `testRestore()`, `shouldRemoveKeysWithNullValues()` |\n| `AbstractKeyValueStoreTest.java` | Base test patterns | `testRestore()`, `testRestoreWithDefaultSerdes()` |\n| `KeyValueStoreTestDriver.java` | Test utility | `addEntryToRestoreLog()`, `restoredEntries()`, `context()` |\n| `InternalMockProcessorContext.java` | Mock context implementation | `restore()`, `register()` |\n| `TimeOrderedKeyValueBufferTest.java` | Restore callback examples | Direct `RecordBatchingStateRestoreCallback.restoreBatch()` usage |\n| `StateRestoreCallbackAdapterTest.java` | Callback adapter patterns | Callback adaptation logic |\n\nAll files are located in `/app/streams/src/test/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/`"}],"totalDurationMs":63614,"totalTokens":79695,"totalToolUseCount":36,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":327,"cache_read_input_tokens":76447,"output_tokens":2921,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":327},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}}}
